# Azure AI: The Big Picture

> The tech world is obviously enamored with artificial intelligence. After decades of research, developers now have a robust set of tools that make it easier to add machine learning or cognitive services to their applications. It’s no surprise that Microsoft is heavily invested in the AI space.This course looks at the big picture of Microsoft Azure AI offerings. Instructor Walt Ritscher provides a p

#### [The Azure AI services names](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] [[Microsoft Azure|Azure]] AI services offer a collection of cloud-based tools that help developers build intelligent applications.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=7)** These services include ready-made and customizable APIs and models, enabling you to add cognitive intelligence to your apps without needing AI or [[Data Science]] skills.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=17)** If you follow [[Microsoft]], you know that they change product and service names periodically.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=22)** Microsoft is constantly evolving and improving its Azure Cloud platform, which includes a wide range of services and features.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=29)** As part of this evolution, Microsoft sometimes renames or rebrands its Azure Services to better reflect their capabilities or to align with industry standards.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=38)** In fact, they have recently made some changes to the names of certain Azure AI services.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=43)** The new general name is Azure AI Services.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=46)** All of the AI services fall under the sensible umbrella name.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=50)** There are a number of these services.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=52)** Within each service are subsets of services.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=55)** They help us narrow down our options, whether you're analyzing text sentiment, recognizing objects and images, or translating languages, Azure AI Services provides the capabilities you need for various scenarios and industries.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=69)** Here's one example of the name evolution.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=71)** Microsoft Bot Framework was a platform for building and deploying chatbots and [[Conversational AI]] applications.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=79)** It provided developers with tools and resources to create bots that could interact with users through various channels such as [[Facebook]] Messenger, Skype, [[Slack]], and more.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=89)** Soon it was integrated into Azure Bot Service, which is a part of Azure AI.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=94)** Azure Bot Service provides a more comprehensive and integrated set of tools for building and deploying bots.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=100)** A few years later, Microsoft categorized it into a group called Azure Applied AI Services.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=106)** For the last few years, Microsoft has grouped the AI services into categories like Cognitive Services and Applied AI Services.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=113)** Microsoft has officially dropped these category names.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=117)** Regardless of the current names, [[Microsoft Azure]]'s AI Services continue to offer powerful capabilities.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-ai-services-names?u=76281980&t=123)** As we go through the course, I'll highlight these changes when relevant.

#### [An overview of Azure AI](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] [[Artificial Intelligence (AI)|Artificial intelligence]] has become one of the most transformative technologies of our time, with the potential to revolutionize the way we create content and work.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=9)** At its core, AI is about creating intelligent machines and software that can perform tasks that would normally require human intelligence, such as recognizing patterns, making decisions, and learning from experience.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=22)** AI technology is changing the way we interact with the world around us.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=25)** Whether it's from machine learning [[Algorithms]] that can analyze vast amounts of data or auto caption services that can parse video and extract captions, we are seeing the massive influence of AI on our lives.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=37)** What do you think of when you hear AI mentioned in conversation?
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=41)** It's a wide area.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=42)** My guess is that it's one of these areas: machine learning, cognitive services, [[Large Language Models (LLM)|large language models]], [[Generative AI]], or the [[IoT|Internet of Things]].
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=53)** Let's start with the difference between artificial intelligence and machine learning.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=57)** Artificial intelligence is the broader concept of creating machines that can perform tasks that typically require human intelligence, such as understanding languages, recognizing images, making decisions, and solving problems.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=70)** Machine learning is a subset of AI that involves training algorithms to learn from data and make predictions or decisions without being explicitly programmed for each task.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=80)** In other words, machine learning is a way to achieve AI.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=83)** It uses statistical techniques to enable machines to improve their performance on a task over time as they're exposed to more data.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=91)** Machine learning is important because it allows software to learn and improve from data.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=95)** This can lead to more accurate and efficient [[Decision-Making]].
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=98)** By analyzing patterns and trends in data, machine learning algorithms can identify insights and make predictions faster than humans.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=106)** For example, say we want to classify music into categories like hip-hop, rock, and dubstep.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=112)** Rather than establishing rules for categorization, developers input thousands of examples of each music genre into the machine learning algorithm.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=121)** The algorithm then identifies patterns within the music and utilizes those characteristics to recognize and catalog other songs.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=128)** Machine learning serves as the fundamental building block of [[Microsoft Azure|Azure]] AI, providing the backbone upon which many of its key features and capabilities are built.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=136)** In machine learning, algorithms are used to analyze data and identify patterns or relationships in that data.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=142)** An AI algorithm is a set of instructions or rules that a computer program follows to perform a specific task.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=149)** It is a step-by-step process that takes input data and produces output data based on a set of rules.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=155)** This collection of algorithms is used to train the AI model.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=159)** The process of training a machine learning model involves feeding it large amounts of data and allowing it to learn from that data over time.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=166)** The algorithm used to train the model will adjust the model's parameters based on the data it receives in order to improve its accuracy and performance.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=175)** Once the model has been trained, it can be used to make predictions or decisions based on new data that it encounters.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=181)** Azure offers a variety of tools and services that allow developers to build, train, and deploy custom machine learning models.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=188)** One way to create custom models in Azure is to use Azure Machine Learning Studio, a web-based development environment for building machine learning models.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=197)** With Azure Machine Learning Studio, developers can drag and drop modules to create a machine learning workflow, and then use the platform to train and deploy their models.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=206)** Another option is to use the Azure Machine Learning Service in the Azure Portal.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=210)** This is more time-consuming for developers and data scientists.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=213)** We'll see more about both of these approaches in the machine learning chapter.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=217)** You don't need to create your own models, however.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=219)** That's because Azure offers a variety of pre-built machine learning models and services, which provide developers with ready-to-use APIs for tests, like image recognition.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=228)** With tools like this, Azure can analyze the contents of images or videos and identify specific content.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=235)** For the last few years, [[Microsoft]] has grouped the AI services into categories like Cognitive Services and Applied AI Services.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=242)** As I mentioned in another video, Microsoft has officially dropped these category names.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=247)** The features are still available, just renamed to Azure AI Services.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=251)** However, it's still common to call the group of services shown here Azure Cognitive Services.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=257)** They are a suite of prebuilt machine learning models and APIs that enable developers to add intelligent features to their applications without needing to build and train their own models from scratch.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=268)** These services provide a range of capabilities, including vision, speech, and language.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=273)** Another subcategory of AI is large language models, or LLMs.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=277)** They are a type of machine learning model that is specifically designed to process and understand natural language.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=284)** While other machine learning models may be designed to process structured data, such as numerical or categorical data, large language models are designed to process [[Unstructured Data]], such as text or speech.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=297)** This requires different techniques and algorithms for processing and analyzing the data.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=301)** LLMs are typically built using [[Deep Learning]] techniques, such as [[Neural Networks]], and are trained on large amounts of text data to learn patterns and relationships in language.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=311)** Some of the Azure cognitive services are based on large language models.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=315)** For example, the Language Understanding service, LUIS, is based on a large language model that has been trained on a vast amount of text data to understand natural language queries and commands.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=326)** LUIS allows developers to build [[Natural Language Processing (NLP)|natural language processing]] capabilities into their applications, enabling users to interact with the application using conversational language.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=334)** Similarly, the Text Analytics service in Azure cognitive services is based on large language models that have been trained on vast amounts of text data to identify sentiment, key phrases, and other insights in the text.
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=348)** This service can be used to analyze customer feedback, social media posts, and other text data to gain insights into customer behavior and preferences.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=356)** One of the most popular pre-trained language models or LLMs is offered by OpenAI, an artificial intelligence research laboratory.
>
> **[6:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=364)** [[ChatGPT]] is a pre-trained language model for [[Conversational AI]] based on the GPT, which stands for generative pre-trained transformer architecture.
>
> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=375)** GPT is a type of neural network.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=378)** ChatGPT is designed to generate human-like responses to natural language queries that can be fine-tuned for specific use cases.
>
> **[6:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=386)** Microsoft is a significant partner with OpenAI, which means that we can use OpenAI models and services from Azure.
>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=393)** AI models can also be paired with generation tools, so the vast amount of information gathered via machine learning can also be used to create new content.
>
> **[6:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=401)** Because of this, machine learning is having a significant impact on the creative world.
>
> **[6:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=407)** For example, machine learning algorithms can be used to generate music, art, and even literature.
>
> **[6:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=412)** They do this by analyzing patterns and styles in existing works and creating new ones based on that analysis.
>
> **[6:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=418)** One popular generative tool is [[DALL-E]], a neural network-based image generation system developed by OpenAI.
>
> **[7:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=425)** It can generate high-quality images from textual descriptions.
>
> **[7:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=429)** This system is trained on a massive data set of images and text, and uses a combination of deep learning techniques to generate images that match the given text description.
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=439)** Because of the Microsoft partnership with OpenAI, we can use DALL-E in our applications.
>
> **[7:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=443)** Finally, let's look at the Internet of Things.
>
> **[7:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=445)** It refers to a group of connected or network set of physical devices, vehicles, home appliances, and other items that are embedded with sensors, software and connectivity.
>
> **[7:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=455)** [[IoT]] is rapidly expanding, with billions of devices already connected to the internet and many more expected to come online in the coming years.
>
> **[7:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=463)** This fast network of connected devices has the potential to transform industries ranging from healthcare and manufacturing to transportation and agriculture.
>
> **[7:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=471)** AI is poised to play a crucial role in unlocking the full potential of the Internet of Things.
>
> **[7:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=476)** By applying machine learning algorithms to the massive amounts of data generated by IoT devices, we can gain deeper insights into patterns and trends, identify anomalies and outliers, and make more accurate predictions.
>
> **[8:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=489)** Azure offers a wide range of AI services, including cognitive services, machine learning, bot services, IoT, and OpenAI.
>
> **[8:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/an-overview-of-azure-ai?u=76281980&t=497)** Overall, Azure provides a comprehensive set of AI services that can be used to build intelligent applications across a wide range of industries and use cases.

>

>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=292)** It can apply content tags for thousands of recognizable objects, living beings, scenery, and action that appear in images.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=300)** Tagging is not limited to the main subject, such as the person in the foreground, but also includes the setting indoors or outdoors, and other items.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=310)** The Azure Anomaly Detector is a service that helps you detect anomalies, unexpected changes in time series data.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=316)** It uses machine learning algorithms to automatically identify patterns and anomalies in your data, and it can be used to detect anomalies in a wide range of applications such as fraud detection, predictive maintenance, and performance monitoring.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=330)** Metrics Advisor is a service built upon the anomaly detector.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=334)** It uses AI to perform data monitoring and anomaly detection in time series data.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=340)** The service automates the process of applying models to your data and provides a set of APIs and a web-based workspace for [[Data Ingestion]], anomaly detection, and diagnostics without needing to know machine learning.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=353)** Azure OpenAI is a partnership between [[Microsoft]] and OpenAI.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=356)** A research organization focused on developing [[Artificial Intelligence (AI)|artificial intelligence]] in a safe and beneficial way.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=362)** As part of the collaboration, some of the OpenAI's language models are available on [[Microsoft Azure]].
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=368)** Here are two examples.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=369)** The most famous model is the one used in [[ChatGPT]], a good example of interactive chat based AI.
>
> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=375)** In Azure OpenAI, we have access to the underlying model called GPT 4 or GPT 3.5.
>
> **[6:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=382)** [[DALL-E]] is an advanced image generation model developed by OpenAI.
>
> **[6:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=386)** It can generate highly realistic images from textual descriptions, allowing users to create images of objects and scenes that don't exist in the real world.
>
> **[6:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=394)** There are some other services.
>
> **[6:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=396)** With Microsoft Genomics, researchers can analyze genomic data in real time, identify genetic variations, and gain insights into the underlying causes of diseases.
>
> **[6:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=405)** Microsoft Bonsai is a platform that enables developers to build and deploy AI models for autonomous systems.
>
> **[6:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=412)** It is designed to make it easier for developers to create and train AI models that can control physical systems such as robots or industrial equipment.
>
> **[7:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=421)** The Azure AI Bot Service is the place to go to build automated bots.
>
> **[7:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=425)** It's especially good at building chatbots.
>
> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=427)** Developers can create chatbots that can interact with users via voice, text, or other natural language interfaces.
>
> **[7:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/a-short-tour-of-the-azure-ai-services?u=76281980&t=434)** Finally, we have the Azure AI Content Safety Service.

>

>

>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=143)** And Azure Machine Learning jobs are training runs that you use to build your models.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=148)** You can group jobs together into experiments to compare metrics.
>

>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=161)** Pipelines are reusable workflows for training and retraining your model.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=165)** The core of a machine learning pipeline is to split the complete machine learning task into multi-step workflow.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=172)** Each step is a manageable component that can be developed or optimized and configured and automated individually.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=179)** Steps are connected through well-defined interfaces.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=182)** The Azure Machine Learning pipeline service automatically orchestrates all the dependencies between the pipeline steps.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=188)** Data assets aid in the management of the data that you use for model training and for your pipeline creation.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=195)** By using data assets, you can easily manage and organize your data and ensure that it is easily accessible for use in the pipelines.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=202)** An Azure Machine Learning data store serves as a reference to an existing Azure storage account.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=209)** Registering a model means that you're creating a reference to a trained machine learning model in your workspace.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=214)** This reference includes [[Metadata]] about the model, such as this name, version, and description, as well as information about the run that produced the model.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=223)** Registering a model allows you to easily track and manage your models and makes it simple to deploy them to production environments.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=230)** Once you have trained your machine learning models or pipelines, it is necessary to deploy them to production so that they can be used for inference.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=238)** In machine learning, inference refers to the process of applying a trained model to new unseen data in order to make predictions or decisions.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=246)** Once a machine learning model has been trained on a set of label data, it can be used to make predictions or decisions on new unlabeled data.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=254)** Inference involves applying new input data to the machine learning model to generate outputs, which are commonly referred to as predictions.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=262)** However, inferencing can also be used to generate outputs for other machine learning tasks, such as classification and clustering.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=270)** In Azure, you can perform inferencing by utilizing endpoints and deployments.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=275)** These endpoints and deployments allow you to separate the interface of your production workload from the implementation that serves it, providing greater flexibility and [[Scalability]].
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=284)** Creating an online endpoint refers to the process of deploying a trained machine learning model as a web service that can be accessed by other applications or services over the internet.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=294)** Creating an online endpoint in Azure Machine Learning involves packaging the trained model as a Docker container, configuring the deployment environment and exposing the endpoint through a [[Representational State Transfer (REST)|REST]] API.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-machine-learning?u=76281980&t=306)** Once the endpoint is up and running, it can be accessed by other applications or services using HTTP requests.

> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=146)** Pipelines are essential for orchestrating and automating various stages of the machine learning lifecycle from data preparation to model training and deployment.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=155)** The environment section is where you define and manage the computing environments that your machine learning experiments and models will run in.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=163)** These environments are crucial for ensuring that your code executes consistently across different stages of the machine learning lifecycle.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=170)** The core component of machine learning is the model.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=173)** The studio has a section for working with your models.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=176)** I'll come back to this topic later in this video.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=178)** The endpoint section is where you manage the deployment of your machine learning models for inference.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=184)** This is where you set up your models to be accessible via an endpoint, allowing them to process new data and make predictions or classifications in real time.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=193)** By deploying models to endpoints, you enable them to perform inference tasks directly from the Azure platform, making it easy to integrate them into applications and your other services.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=205)** To interact with Azure Machine Learning, you need a computer, either your own or one in the cloud.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=211)** This is known as compute in machine learning.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=214)** For development purposes, Azure Machine Learning provides compute instances which are interactive and come with pre-configured environments, making them ideal for [[Data Science]] tasks.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=224)** However, for model training, which may require more powerful and expensive resources, compute clusters are used.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=232)** These clusters are managed by Azure Machine Learning to start and stop as needed, ensuring you only pay for the compute resources when they are in use.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=240)** The monitoring section is a key feature that allows us to keep track of the performance and behavior of our machine learning models and experiments.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=249)** The data labeling section is designed to help us create, manage, and monitor data labeling projects.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=255)** Data labeling in machine learning is the process of annotating raw data such as images, text, or videos with meaningful labels that provide context.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=265)** These labels help machine learning models understand and learn from the data.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=270)** For example, in an image dataset, labels might identify objects like pizza, sandwich, or burrito.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=277)** Let's say you decide to use the Machine Learning Studio and you want to work with your models.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=282)** To harness this potential, several key steps are involved.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=285)** Choosing the training data, choosing a model algorithm, and creating the model.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=290)** Training it on your data, evaluating its validity, and then deploying it for real world use.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=296)** The studio simplifies this process offering a comprehensive platform for these steps and more.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=302)** The studio provides a variety of tools for feature engineering, which involves selecting and transforming the most relevant features in your data to improve the performance of your machine learning models.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=312)** The studio includes a feature called Automated Machine Learning, which allows us to automatically select the best algorithm and hyper parameters for the machine learning tasks.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=322)** Once you have trained your machine learning models, you can use the studio to deploy them to production.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=328)** This includes setting up endpoints and deploying models to Azure, [[Kubernetes]], or Azure container instance.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=334)** Let's talk about another similar name tool.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=336)** It's the [[Azure AI Studio]], which is sometimes called the Azure OpenAI Studio.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=342)** It is another web-based interface that allows you to interact with the Azure OpenAI service.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=347)** Here, you can use the playground to experiment with the services capabilities by submitting prompts and generating completions.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=354)** You can also use it to manage your deployment and models.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=357)** Here, you can see the playground section listed on the left menu bar.
>
> **[6:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=361)** Here, you can use the chat services or use the [[DALL-E]] generative service to create images.
>
> **[6:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/azure-machine-learning-studio?u=76281980&t=366)** We'll look at the Azure AI Studio in another chapter.

#### [Build better prompts with Prompt Flow](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the realm of [[Large Language Models (LLM)|large language models]], a prompt refers to a natural language instruction or query given to the model.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=7)** The purpose of the prompt is to guide the model in generating a response that is both correct and adequate in form and content.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=15)** Crafting a good prompt is a critical skill, because it ensures that you receive accurate and specific results.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=21)** Without this skill, you may end up with vague or inaccurate responses.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=25)** [[Prompt Engineering]] is the name given to the skill of crafting effective prompts.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=30)** There is a lot of buzz about large language model prompt engineering, because it is an emerging field that requires creativity and attention to detail.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=38)** It involves selecting the right words, phrases, and formats to guide the model into generating high-quality and relevant information.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=46)** Whether you are using [[ChatGPT]] to casually write some social media headlines for your TikTok account or using [[Microsoft Azure|Azure]] LLMs to get report data from your enterprise data sources, writing a good prompt is an iterative process requiring thought and refinement.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=62)** There are several steps to think about.
>

>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=65)** What do you want the model to generate?
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=67)** In this case, I want a summary of a certain published medical paper.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=72)** So my first prompt in ChatGPT simply states that goal.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=76)** In ChatGPT, I'd run the query and see the initial results.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=80)** Perhaps I get back a one-sentence answer, which is accurate but too short.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=84)** In the Azure scenario, the data scientist goes through a similar process.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=89)** After the initial prompt is entered into the language model, the response is analyzed.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=93)** The model may generate an accurate but limited result, perhaps lacking the specific angle needed for a report.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=100)** With the insights gathered from testing and analysis, it's time to revisit the prompt.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=105)** This could involve making it more specific, adding more context, or changing the phrasing.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=110)** In this ChatGPT scenario, I'd refine it by requesting a four-paragraph summary.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=116)** I also apply some guidance on the expected writing style.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=119)** Creating effective prompts using LLMs is a crucial aspect of generating high-quality content, but it can be challenging and frustrating.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=127)** This prompt engineering process involves several steps, such as preparing the data, creating the tailored prompts, executing the prompts using the LLM API, and then refining the generated content.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=139)** [[Microsoft]] created the Azure Machine Learning [[Prompt Flow]] to streamline the entire development cycle of AI applications that are powered by LLMs.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=147)** It streamlines the development, evaluation, and the [[Continuous Integration (CI)|continuous integration]] and deployment of prompt engineering projects.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=154)** It empowers data scientists and the LLM application developers with an interactive experience that combines natural language prompts, templating language, and a list of built-in tools and [[Python (Programming Language)|Python]] code.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=166)** The Azure research team found some significant blocking points in the workflow, which convinced Microsoft to create prompt flow.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=173)** Here are some of the main challenges grouped into three categories.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=176)** First is design and development.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=178)** Users must understand LLMs, experiment with different prompt, and use complex logic and [[Control Flow]] to create effective prompts.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=187)** They also may face something called a cold start problem where they lack prior knowledge or examples to guide them.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=193)** Second, we have evaluation and refinement.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=196)** Users must ensure that the outputs are consistent, helpful, honest, and harmless, avoiding potential biases and pitfalls.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=205)** They also must define and measure prompt quality and effectiveness using standard metrics.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=211)** Finally, we have optimization and production.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=213)** Users must monitor and troubleshoot prompt issues, compare and improve prompt variance, optimize prompt length without compromising performance, deal with token limitations, and secure their prompts from injection attacks.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=225)** They must also collaborate with other developers and ensure stability over large data volumes.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=230)** You can find prompt flow in the Azure Machine Learning Studio.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=234)** Here is an example screenshot from the Microsoft documentation.

>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/build-better-prompts-with-prompt-flow?u=76281980&t=280)** And then last, it uses a Python script to convert LLM output into a dictionary.

>

>

>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=38)** It is a type of language model that uses [[Deep Learning]] technology to understand and generate human-like text.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=45)** It supports tasks such as [[Content Creation]], language translation, programming assistance, and more.

>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=55)** Codex is a language model designed to assist with programming tasks.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=59)** It can generate code snippets based on natural language prompts and supports multiple programming languages, including [[Python (Programming Language)|Python]], [[JavaScript]], and more.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=67)** It powers [[GitHub Copilot]], an AI-powered code completion tool that helps developers write code more efficiently by suggesting whole lines or blocks of code.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=76)** Whisper is a model that can transcribe audio into text across multiple languages.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=80)** CLIP is a model that can understand and match images with text descriptions.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=85)** It can identify what an image represents based on a natural language prompt and perform tasks like image classification without needing additional training for specific tasks.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=95)** Embeddings is a set of models that can convert text into a numerical form that machine learning models can understand.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=101)** Moderation is a fine-tuned model that can detect whether text may be sensitive or unsafe.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=106)** These models are designed to help automatically detect and filter harmful or inappropriate content in text.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=112)** As you can deduce from that list, OpenAI and Azure have some comparable services.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=118)** What's new is that Microsoft has partnered with OpenAI, which means that we can use the OpenAI models from Azure.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=124)** This is exciting for many developers as there's a growing consensus that OpenAI has some of the best models available.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=130)** There is a cost to this of course, and not every service has a direct equivalent.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=134)** For example, there is no DALL-E type service yet in the native Azure AI.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=140)** Azure OpenAI service is a service that provides [[Representational State Transfer (REST)|REST]] API access to open AI's powerful language models, including [[GPT-4]], Embeddings, DALL-E, and Whisper.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=151)** These models can be easily adapted to your specific task, including but not limited to content generation, summarization, [[Semantic Search]], and natural language to code translation.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=162)** We can access the services through REST APIs, the Python SDK, or the web-based interface in the Azure OpenAI Studio.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=170)** By including it within Azure, we get the advanced language models combined with the security and enterprise promise of Azure.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-basics-of-azure-openai-service?u=76281980&t=176)** The Azure team co-develop the APIs with OpenAI, ensuring compatibility and a smooth transition from one to the other.

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-studios?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] [[Microsoft Azure|Azure]] offers a variety of tools for interacting with its services, including the Azure [[CLI]], Azure [[Powershell]], Azure [[Representational State Transfer (REST)|REST]] APIs, and the Azure web portal.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/the-azure-studios?u=76281980&t=11)** The Azure Portal has long been the primary web interface for creating, configuring, and managing all available Azure services.
>

>

#### [Explore the features of Azure AI language analysis](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] [[Microsoft Azure|Azure]] AI Language service is a comprehensive suite of [[Natural Language Processing (NLP)|natural language processing]] tools designed to help developers build intelligent applications that understand and interpret human language.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=12)** We can learn more about them on the Azure AI Language Studio site.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=16)** One of the key features of Azure AI Language service is its text analytics capabilities, which enable applications to analyze text for sentiment, key phrases, named entities, and language detection.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=28)** Language detection is a feature that identifies the language of a given text input.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=33)** It can automatically determine the language of a text from over 120 languages.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=37)** The language detection process involves analyzing text to identify the most likely language, considering various linguistic patterns, structures, and characteristics unique to each language.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=48)** This functionality is powered by advanced machine learning models trained on a vast dataset of multilingual content.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=55)** The feature can handle a wide range of text lengths and is robust enough to manage both formal and informal language.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=62)** Key phrase extraction is a feature that automatically identifies and extracts the most important phrases from a block of texts.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=69)** This tool helps developers and businesses quickly determine the key topics or themes in large volumes of text data, such as documents, customer reviews, emails, or social media posts.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=81)** By pinpointing key phrases, the service enables sufficient data analysis, allows us to identify trends and gain valuable insights without manually sifting through extensive text.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=90)** Azure AI language offers a PII or personally identifiable information feature that identifies, categorizes, and redacts sensitive information, such as phone numbers, email addresses, and many [[Forms]] of identification.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=105)** Azure Text Analytics for Health is a specialized feature designed to process and analyze medical and clinical text.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=112)** It leverages the natural language processing to extract valuable information such as electronic health records, clinical notes, and medical literature.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=122)** It can identify and categorize critical medical information, including diagnosis, symptoms, medications, and treatment procedures.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=131)** Use text summarization to generate concise summaries from plain text, whether from a document, conversation, or other text source.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=139)** This API provides two summarization approaches.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=142)** Extractive summarization creates a summary by selecting key sentences directly from the original text along with their positional information.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=150)** Extractive summarization identify sentences that best represent the main idea of the document and ranks them based on their relevance to the primary topic.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=159)** For example, if a three-sentence summary is requested, the API returns to top three highest scoring sentences.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=166)** The extractive sentences are original, unaltered segments from the input content, and the positional information includes the starting point and length of each sentence within the text.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=175)** Abstractive summarization generates a summary using new sentences or phrases that are not directly taken from the input text.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=183)** It produces concise and coherent summaries that captures the essence of the original content.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=187)** Sentiment analysis is used to determine the emotional tone or sentiment expressed in a piece of text.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=193)** It identifies and categorize feelings such as positive, negative, neutral, or sometimes more specific emotions like happy, sad, angry, or surprised.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=202)** Opinion mining, also known as aspect-based sentiment analysis, is a type of sentiment analysis that digs deeper into specific opinions in the text.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-features-of-azure-ai-language-analysis?u=76281980&t=212)** It identifies and analyzes sentiments related to features or aspects of [[Microsoft Products|products]] and services, providing a detailed view of what people think about different elements.

#### [Explore the built-in voice agents](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=6)** These agents are divided into two categories, built-in agents and customizable voice agents.

>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=46)** One of the key advantages of Azure's agents is their ability to handle complex linguistic nuances.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=53)** The AI models behind these agents are trained on vast amounts of data, enabling them to produce speech that accurately reflects the intended tone, emotion, and context.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=63)** This capability is crucial for applications that require expressive and dynamic speech, such as audio books, educational content, and interactive [[Storytelling]].
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=73)** By capturing the subtleties of human speech, Azure's agents can deliver a more engaging and immersive [[User Experience (UX)|user experience]].
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=80)** If the current set of voice agents doesn't have what you need, you can train your own.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=84)** Customizable voice agents offer a higher degree of personalization.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/explore-the-built-in-voice-agents?u=76281980&t=88)** With Azure's neural text to speech technology, developers can create custom voices that reflect their brand's unique identity.
>

> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=163)** It can extract text, page headers, titles, section headers, paragraphs, tables like we mentioned, figures, the page footer, the page number, and so on.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=174)** It's also able to determine selection marks, which is to say that it can determine whether the user marked or checked a checkbox.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=182)** Microsoft provides a set of prebuilt models for common form structures.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=186)** Supported documents include receipts, invoices, business cards, identity documents, vaccination cards, US health insurance cards, and tax forms.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=197)** It can also extract key value pairs, which are specific sections within a document that consist of a label, the key, and its corresponding response, the value.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=206)** In structured forms, these pairs often represent the label of a field, such as address, and the value entered by the user.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=214)** In unstructured documents, key value pairs can be extracted from the context, such as identifying the execution date of a contract from a sentence within a paragraph.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=223)** Here, we are looking at the main page on another studio.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=226)** This is called the Document Intelligence Studio.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=228)** And I want to point out the three boxes on the top that show the basic types of analysis you can do on your documents.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=233)** You can read the contents of the documents and get the text.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=237)** You can also look at the layout of the document and find out where there are tables, and check boxes, and so on.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/streamline-data-extraction-with-azure-document-intelligence?u=76281980&t=242)** And then the third option is what's called General Documents.

#### [Detect anomalies with Azure Metrics Advisor](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/detect-anomalies-with-azure-metrics-advisor?u=76281980)

>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/unlock-smarter-search-with-azure-cognitive-search?u=76281980&t=192)** For example, assuming that dog, canine, puppy, and pooch are mapped synonyms, a query on canine will match on a document containing dog.
>

>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/unlock-smarter-search-with-azure-cognitive-search?u=76281980&t=208)** This is helpful when dealing with data that may contain typos or misspellings.

>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/unlock-smarter-search-with-azure-cognitive-search?u=76281980&t=223)** Fuzzy matching can be used to match words that have different spellings in different regions.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/unlock-smarter-search-with-azure-cognitive-search?u=76281980&t=227)** For example, the different spelling of the word color in the UK and the US should still result in finding the correct data in the dataset.

>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/unlock-smarter-search-with-azure-cognitive-search?u=76281980&t=273)** For example, when you search for shoes on an online shopping website, you can filter your results by selecting different facets to find exactly what you are looking for.

> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/unlock-smarter-search-with-azure-cognitive-search?u=76281980&t=282)** Are you tired of building search functionality from scratch every time you start a new project?

> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=99)** Because it's built on [[Microsoft Azure|Azure]], it includes features such as encryption of data at [[Representational State Transfer (REST)|rest]] and in transit, access controls and auditing capabilities to ensure that data is secure and compliant with industry standards.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=110)** Azure also has a comprehensive set of compliance offerings, including certifications for the US Health Insurance Portability and [[Accountability]] Act, also known as HIPAA.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=120)** It's also GDPR compliant and supports many other certifications.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=125)** Genomics has many real world applications.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=127)** Cancer genomics is how we study changes in a person's DNA that can lead to the development of cancer, as well as how this information can be used to develop more effective cancer treatments.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=137)** Infectious disease genomics is the study of how genomics can be used to understand the genetic makeup of infectious agents, such as viruses and bacteria, and how this information can be used to develop more effective treatments.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=149)** Pharmacogenomics is the study of how an individual's genetic makeup affects their response to drugs, including how they metabolize drugs and how they may experience side effects.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=158)** Instead of managing your own data centers, take advantage of the scale and experience of Microsoft at running global scale workloads.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/azure-ai-the-big-picture-23676334/reveal-genetic-insights-with-microsoft-genomics?u=76281980&t=165)** Their cloud inflammation is designed to be highly compatible with the best practices pipeline used by medical research institutes, and it's used by research hospitals, like Seattle Children's Hospital to create high quality genomic datasets for pediatric diseases.
